Case of a Child Killed by a Car

Witnesses Testify in Court

Judge Orders Plaintiff to Withdraw and Await Further Inquiry

The eight-year-old son of Mrs. Gao Huang, a resident of Rue Bourgeat in the French Concession, was cooling off in front of her house at 6:00 PM on July 27th when he was negligently hit and killed by a car driven by a Western woman, Mrs. Lapeina Veshuit. The victim's family hired lawyer Fei Xizhen to file a lawsuit in the French Court. The plaintiff, Gao Huang, testified that her son was tragically killed and requested justice. Witness Huang Longqi stated that the deceased was his nephew and was sitting next to a large tree in front of the door that evening, cooling off. Gao was also sitting in front of number 326. He witnessed the defendant's car, driven by a Western woman from west to east, with another Westerner sitting next to her, instructing the driver, which led to negligence. The car ran onto the sidewalk, first knocking down the barber Zhou Jinyun, and then hitting the nephew next to the big tree. He immediately rushed forward to pick him up, but his leg was broken and he was dying. He immediately hired a taxi to take him to the hospital. Witness Yu Hanzhang testified that he was also sitting there cooling off that evening and saw the defendant's car with license plate number 573, a red license plate, driving back and forth on the road. It was driven by a Western woman, with a foreign man instructing her. To avoid a rickshaw in front, the car ran off the road and hit Zhou Jinyun and the child.

The person in the car got out, took off the license plate, and tried to escape, but was stopped by onlookers. Zhou Jinyun testified that he worked at a barber shop at number 328 Rue Bourgeat and was cooling off in front of the door that day. The defendant's car came from behind, first knocking him down and then hitting the plaintiff's child, causing his death. He suffered only minor injuries and was not seriously hurt. The plaintiff's lawyer then argued for a long time. The Chinese and Western judges ordered them to withdraw and await further inquiry and verification.

Driver Fined 20 Yuan

Mrs. Deng Huaide, a Western woman, filed a complaint with the French Court yesterday, stating that she was on her way home from her office the day before and hired a rickshaw pulled by Wu Guitang. The Chinese and Western judges sentenced Sun to a fine of 20 yuan or 20 days in prison as a warning. The plaintiff's request for compensation was directed to a civil lawsuit.

Death Caused by Scratching Sha

Fine of 130 Yuan

Civil Lawsuit Orders Compensation of 300 Yuan

Wang Zhenhua, a Wuxi native and owner of a barber shop at 920 Rue Macgregor, was arrested by the police and brought to the Special District Local Court for causing the death of Cheng Jingkui by scratching sha and puncturing his arm with a needle, causing poisoning. The deceased's wife, Zhang, also filed a lawsuit against Wang, seeking 3,000 yuan in damages. This was previously reported in the newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Sun Yuan continued the trial and sentenced Wang Zhenhua to a fine of 130 yuan for causing death due to negligence in his business. The number of days of detention were allowed to be offset by a fine of two yuan per day of detention. In the civil suit portion, Wang Zhenhua was ordered to pay 300 yuan in compensation. During the appeal period, the defendant was allowed to post 500 yuan bail, and the medicinal needles were confiscated.

Zheng Xingmin Missing

Weather Report

The Zikawei Observatory's meteorological forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the Yangtze River basin would be cloudy with rain or fog, and the wind would be from the southeast to southwest. This is due to a low pressure system that has formed in Jiangxi and is moving towards the northeast. There is a southeast wind south of Ma'anshan Island, and a south to southwest wind along the Shandong coast. Also, the temperature in this city for the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday was a high of 73.4 and a low of 64.2. On the same day last year, the high was 78.8 and the low was 58.0.

Letter to the Editor

Dear Editor,

I read in your newspaper on the 24th and 25th that the Soviet Union is selling goods at reduced prices in the markets of Britain and the United States, especially wheat. This has been exposed by various countries, which are trying to stop it. Washington has banned imports, and the German government in Berlin has also ordered a tax increase. However, America is blaming others, and in the past two weeks, it has sold no less than a hundred tons of Chinese factories, causing rice and wheat prices to be affected. If we do not petition for measures to stop this, our farmers will suffer greatly. Therefore, on the 24th, we sent a telegram to the Party and government agencies in Nanjing, Zhenjiang, and Shanghai. On September 24th and 25th, the Shen Bao reported that London telegrams said that the Soviet Union was selling goods at reduced prices in various countries, especially wheat. The Washington telegrams also said the same. This is nothing more than an attempt to cause chaos in order to promote its communist policies. The League of Nations Economic Committee and US Senator Vaudie have exposed its conspiracy and are considering increasing taxes or banning imports, which is a very good method. However, America is blaming others, and in the past two weeks, it has sold no less than a hundred tons of Chinese factories. Other countries will inevitably follow suit, causing rice prices to be very cheap despite the abundant harvest in various provinces. The impact is unknown. We have long admired your enthusiasm for agricultural administration and believe that you will make plans early. We dare to ask you to quickly take measures to stop this, so as to avoid hurting farmers due to low grain prices and to prevent the Communist bandits from taking the opportunity to succeed. We pray for this.

Respectfully,

Representatives of Farmers from Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, and Hunan residing in Shanghai, Chen Guoxian, Zhang Zhijun, Xu Dajun, Gu Zongcheng, Yang Zixiong, 530 people.

Free Talk

Dismissed with a Laugh

— Sea Guest

Woman A—Your love with Mr. G is very deep. You two were very passionate. Why have you become cold to him lately?

Woman B—He is unbearable to be around like that. Just because I was affectionate to him, he became very complacent. He became so happy that he'd get fat, and was gradually going to become a big fat man. Therefore, I've cooled him down a bit to make him depressed, annoyed, and thin out. When he returns to his original state, I will be nice to him again.

Chemistry Teacher (asking the students)—Do you know what method can be used to keep milk from going bad and sour?

Student—Teacher, drink it all in one gulp. That way, it will be fresh, will not go bad, and will not go sour.

Customer (after paying the bill, asking the waiter for change. The waiter acts like he can't calculate the amount)—You are too bad at calculations. How can you not even calculate such a small amount?

Waiter—Sir, the customers here are all very generous. After they eat, they always pay twice the amount of the bill and never ask for change. So we don't need to practice calculations.

A—I have made up my mind. If our manager does not take back what he said, I will leave immediately.

B—Did he insult you with what he said?

A—He told me to find another job.

Anecdotes of Tan Zuchang

— Master of Yiyi Cottage

Tan Zuchang, the former chairman of the National Government, suddenly passed away from a stroke. Everyone who heard of it felt sorrow. The newspapers in both Shanghai and Nanjing published detailed accounts of his life. I suddenly remembered a few things and hastily recorded them below. I dare not say that this is a comprehensive understanding of Tan.

Tan's original name was Tingkai. He became a Jinshi after achieving first place in the provincial examination. At that time, printing houses widely circulated examination papers for candidates to study and emulate. Those preparing for the imperial examination almost all had one of these compilations in hand, much like what we call speculation today. Tan's essays were naturally recited by everyone and sung in every household. I still keep this essay to this day. The topic seemed to be from the first chapter of the Great Learning. After the Qing Dynasty was overthrown, Tan served as the military governor of Hunan Province, and then changed his name to Yankai.

Tan was skilled in calligraphy. His style resembled that of Weng Tonghe, but lacked his elegance, while surpassing him in strength. In the past, when he lived in Shanghai, he had many social engagements. Countless people from my hometown asked for his calligraphy, numbering in the dozens. Two years ago, he had a new seal made, marking his works as done after fifty. This shows that even though he was busy with public affairs, his interest in calligraphy did not wane. Who would have thought that this seal would only last two years before his life ended? How lamentable!

One year, I was traveling in Hangzhou and staying at room 53 on the lower floor of the Qingtai Second Inn. Someone who knew Tan told me, "Tan Zuchang has come to seek lodging." I went out to look and saw Tan wearing a regular top hat, a black jacket, and a white shirt, holding a foreign umbrella, accompanied by several friends, going upstairs one after another. It was said that he was about to resume his post as military governor of Hunan. His appearance was not as refined as the photos sold in the market, nor as plump as he is today. Among his friends was a burly man whom people identified as the Minister of Justice, Zhang Yaozeng. I don't know if this is true. That evening, Tan and his party stayed in room 53 upstairs. The noise of their laughter and conversation, the calling of servants, continued past midnight. Unable to sleep peacefully, I left the next morning.

Tan had several poems about miscellaneous affairs in Guangzhou, filled with sadness and passion. Although I don't remember the year, judging by the tone and meaning, they must have been written after the Second Revolution of 1913. At that time, Yuan Shikai was seizing power and heroes were scattered everywhere. The poem says: "Banana trees fill the shade by the wall, banyan trees cover the pond. The spring flowers bloom red on the kapok branches. Coming again to the courtyard, everything is unfamiliar. Only the setting sun seems like old times." Another poem says: "Wearing a hat and sword, I remember raising a cup. At that time, official duties were a warning against neglect. No one recognizes what happened twenty years ago. With tears, I pass Guangyi Hall again." The meaning is implied in the words. Who would have thought that success would come in just a few years? Living in glory and dying in sorrow, as it is now. For someone like Tan, it can be said that he had no regrets.

Trivial Notes on the Memorial Service for Mr. Yuan Guanlan

— Cailiang

Mr. Yuan Guanlan of Baoshan was a renowned figure in the educational field. His morality and writings were long admired by the literati. He once worked in the Ministry of Education and made many plans. He was especially known for his achievements in compulsory education. In recent years, he retired to Shanghai, engaging in writing and compiling historical materials. His contribution was particularly great. Unfortunately, he contracted a minor illness last month and suddenly passed away. How could it be that his great work was unfinished and his experience was gone? Thinking of his legacy, I feel deep sorrow. Recently, various organizations such as the Shanghai Chinese Vocational Education Society held a memorial service at the Shanghai South Workers' Education Center. The solemn procession was quite a sight. I will now record what I saw and heard in a disorganized manner as follows.

Dedicated to Education: Chairman Cai Yuanpei began the report, saying, "I had a friendly relationship with Mr. Yuan as colleagues. Our friendship can be described as inseparable. I still remember when I worked in the Ministry of Education, I relied heavily on his assistance. The May Fourth Movement suddenly arose, creating a storm. The Ministry of Education was at the forefront and found it difficult to cope. Fortunately, Mr. Yuan mediated and ran around, tirelessly. The student movement was eventually calmed. Furthermore, the nationalization of Tongji University was achieved after several negotiations. All of this was due to Mr. Yuan's leadership. Later, Mr. Yuan resigned from his position because he was not accustomed to political life and went abroad. He visited advanced countries in Europe and America to study educational reforms. After returning to China, he shared his insights with others. His writings amounted to hundreds of thousands of words, and his words were all to the point. This spirit of diligent study and his dedication to his work are truly worthy of emulation for all time and will be remembered forever."

Admirable Thrift: Mr. Zhang Zhongren continued with a speech, saying, "Although Mr. Yuan held senior positions and important posts throughout his life, he lived very frugally and had no bureaucratic airs. Mr. Yuan was content with simplicity and did not seek fame or fortune, unlike the usual officials who liked to elevate their status, give orders, indulge in their desires. These difficult and chaotic times are not without cause. As the saying goes, 'Thrift can foster integrity.' Look at Mr. Yuan; he can inspire."

Penetrating Insights: Mr. Huang Renzhi concluded with a speech, "For decades, our country's education has lacked effectiveness. Education cannot be integrated with society, which is a serious problem. Every time I see farmers' and workers' children who have received education, they are unwilling to return to their original occupations, leading to increased unemployment and harming society. I have also heard that many members of the Communist Party are students who have received secondary or higher education, which is very worrying for the future of education. I once heard Mr. Yuan had a solution: 'The compulsory education I advocate must first ensure that those who receive education do not abandon their original occupations. Then, they can learn and apply what they have learned, complementing each other. Only then can we be innocent of harming society and achieve the true value of education.' I sincerely hope that those who continue Mr. Yuan's work will reflect on these words."

Eulogies: There were many eulogies from various parties, full of beautiful words. I will record those I remember for my friends. Chen Taoyi's eulogy said, "Living in the world for sixty-five years, donating everything from head to toe, like Mozi. Passing away in an instant, coming and going freely, like Zhonglang." Jiang Weiqiao's eulogy said, "Sacrificing his life for education, alas, it is difficult to live in this corrupt world. Suffering from unwarranted criticism in old age, not suffering from incurable diseases. Who would have expected this person to die suddenly, without even seeing him at the end." Wu Yan's eulogy said, "Educational bureaucrats or educators, right or wrong, can be concluded after death. A warm heart, an ancient way, both honest and kind, as inscribed on the tomb, my words will not change." Shen Enfu's eulogy said, "Despising food and clothing, excelling in officialdom and scholarship, diligently serving the country and managing the family, not only appropriate for offering sacrifices to the community. Laboring hard all his life, dying in poverty, using integrity to inspire the weak, not just satirizing the current talents." Pan Wen'an's eulogy said, "Seeking education to be universal, advocating simple learning. Mr. Meng Jinru, his full of enthusiasm. Treating people with kindness and consideration, serving with hunger and drowning in mind. Responsible for those who die later, all should sacrifice this full spirit." I will omit the rest.

Still a Dreamer in the Spring City

— Shuomi

Wandering the world, it has been twenty years. Although I have enjoyed wine and poetry, and sought flowers and willows, the foreign flowers and birds still tug at my heart from time to time. But my temples are gradually gray, and my worldly heart is dead. I no longer have the old ways of a madman. Resting briefly by the sea, surrounded by the stench and noise, I feel that there is no space to pass the time. In my spare time, I only go to the cinema for two hours of entertainment. But it is extremely boring. I still remember those ten years in Beijing, rushing through the pleasure grounds, full of high spirits. How could I have known that there would be today. Not to mention what I have personally experienced, but just the strange sights I have seen and the extraordinary deeds I have heard are both worthy of song and tears, laughter and pity. Sometimes when I think back, I truly feel that strange fun arises. I regret that I am not a novelist and cannot use a vivid pen to describe it in detail for the appreciation of the public. I always consider this a great regret in my life. Since entering autumn, I have been suffering from illness and have moved into the hospital to recuperate. The film, which I relied on as my only source of entertainment, has been temporarily abandoned. The sickbed is lonely, so I read recent novels to pass the time. Yesterday, a friend gave me a copy of the New Classic of Mountains and Seas, a set of five thick volumes. At first, I suspected it was a book of strange tales, but then I saw it labeled as a long social erotic novel and the latest work by Zhang Qiuchong. So I tentatively accepted it and read it. I knew that Zhang was a famous novelist in Shanghai, his works sharp and profound, full of sadism and wildness. I had also heard people say that Zhang was wild and unrestrained in his youth, full of talent and arrogant. His novels cannot be compared with ordinary new books on the market. So I spent three days reading it and finally believed that the pen of a writer is so marvelous that it cannot be measured by ordinary people. The book describes seven romantic figures, prostitutes and actors cunning, officials and their families absurd, warlords and markets. It is dazzling. All the secrets that I have seen and heard, as well as the erotic secrets that I have not seen or heard, are all recorded on paper. It is so wonderful. Sometimes it is beautiful women, sometimes it is bull demons and snake gods, dripping with powder and rubbing with butter, painting dragons and catching ghosts. It fully captures the essence, making the reader sometimes surprised, sometimes happy, sometimes angry, sometimes exclaiming in wonder, sometimes slamming the table and shouting, sometimes feeling as if they are in the book, unknowingly enchanted. It can be called divine skill. The wonder lies in that even the most ordinary little things, once described by the author, become humorous and strange, making people unable to help but laugh. The old dreams of the Spring City are revisited. After reading it repeatedly while sick, I love it so much that I can't bear to let it go. So I write it down to share with my friends.

Editorial Note: The New Classic of Mountains and Seas is my friend Zhang Qiuchong's first masterpiece. Zhang is full of amazing talent and has a great reputation. This book is especially carefully written and extraordinary. The entire book is more than 500,000 words, in five thick volumes, and includes fifty exquisitely colored illustrations by the famous painter Lu Shaofei. The list price is five yuan, but the special price is only three yuan. It is available at the Guanhua Bookstore, Modern Bookstore, and United Bookstore on Fourth Road, as well as the Central Bookstore in the Maijiaquan area.

Publishing News: The Drama Monthly, edited by Liu Gehu of the Datong Bookstore, is the only specialized book on drama in contemporary society. It has been published for two years and has a good reputation. The Mei Lanfang and Shang Xiaoyun issues were especially praised by all sectors. Cheng Yanqiu is an outstanding and eccentric figure in the performing arts, with profound achievements and a talent for creating new tunes. He works in the same field as Mei and Shang but has different styles, each excelling in their own areas. Therefore, it is necessary to publish a special issue. Those who have articles about Cheng to submit to the journal will be paid generously. However, they must be delivered within half a month, as it may be too late to be included. The journal is currently selling short-term pre-orders for Volume 3, with gramophones and records as gifts to enhance interest. The deadline is October 10th.

Correspondence from Europe (75)

— Liu Haisu

Pilgrimage to Italy Diary

(2) En Route A

At 10 p.m. on May 29, we departed from the Gare de Lyon in Paris. It was the beginning of summer, and the days were very long. The sun had just set when we started our journey. Accompanying me were Wu Hengqin, Yang Xiutao, Yan Wenliang, and Sun Fuxi. We traveled southeast, passing through Savoia and crossing the White Peak into Italy. In the train compartment, everyone chatted casually about the itinerary and expenses after arriving in Rome. We elected Xiutao to manage the money and Fuxi to keep the accounts. Later, Fuxi became excited and began to talk about his love story with Ms. Chen Xuezhao. He said, "How passionate and sweet we were at first. But in the end, it was misunderstood for some unknown reason. People thought she had abandoned me. But I didn't value her that much. Even if I had wholeheartedly supported her, it would have only been for decoration. Love, romance, where is it? Perhaps sex is not something that exists in the human world. I always feel that women are fragile, fickle, and inevitably vain and confused. Perhaps there are no women worth loving..." So he was prepared not to marry or talk about love. At that time, I also advised him, "Don't be too biased. It can't be generalized. Women may not be so simple. Besides, 'love' is inherently 'imperfect' and there is nothing to expect as a result..." He waited for a while and then said, "Later, Ms. Chen had a misunderstanding with Mr. G. He felt sorry for her and suddenly wrote her a letter. One day in Paris, he started to visit her again, wanting to ask her what happened. Unexpectedly, after meeting, she scolded him, 'You filthy thing. I don't have time to talk to you and I don't have the mood to correspond with you.' She really thought too highly of herself. She not only misunderstood me but also misunderstood herself." I replied, "Misunderstanding is art. Being able to be misunderstood is great. I ultimately believe that we don't need to be understood. It's better to be misunderstood." Fuxi said, "So you suffer. Many people misunderstand you. Only now do I know your character. Ah, from now on, I will also be bold and rebellious like you. Originally, the articles I wrote before, the paintings I painted before, were not my true self. You see, from now on..."

"Yes, we only need to be honest and unpretentious, moving in the direction that our heart wants to move. If you want to swim, you have to tighten your body and jump into the water. We are inherently traitors to tradition and sinners to the world. I cannot perfunctorily compromise. I cannot compromise and follow the old ways. I am a fool who is used to being ridiculed. But I am willing to be a fool for life, following the power of my internal life. The reason why China is the way it is now is because there are too many people with petty tricks and petty abilities. So society has become so frivolous and ungrateful. I think you also have some foolishness. I hope you become a fool. I don't want you to be a rat-like, petty-minded person." This is what I excitedly told Fuxi at the time.

The Anti-Communist Movement of Finnish Farmers

— Liu Zeng, residing in Paris

In reality, the existence and activities of these 23 Communist Party members in the parliament cannot create any revolutionary danger. However, the government is concerned that the Communist Party's propaganda will spread further and that a portion of the population will be exploited. In addition, there is also various assistance from neighboring Russia, which will make things difficult for the government. Therefore, it is necessary to actively resolve the Communist Party issue.

The government's attitude towards suppressing the Communist Party coincides with the attitude of the Finnish farmers. There are no large farms in Finland. The Finnish farming class is entirely composed of small farmers. These small farmers tend to be conservative, serious, and hardworking. They are not very concerned about political and social matters, but they are very patriotic. Moreover, the area around Central Ostrobothnia, where the Lapua Movement originated, has a strong religious influence. Communist propaganda is detrimental to religion. Therefore, the prevailing religious ideas in the area further fueled the farmers' aversion to the Communist Party. Furthermore, during the Finnish War of Independence, the majority of the army was composed of the farming class. The farmers shed much blood for their country. Now, they see that the achievements of their bloody battles are threatened with destruction by Communist propaganda. Their patriotic and anti-communist sentiments naturally arise. For years, the farmers have tried their best to tolerate and avoid conflict with the Communist Party. However, their feelings of resentment have accumulated deeper and deeper, just like a volcano about to erupt.

The first place where this volcano erupted was Lapua. Communist Party members in Lapua imitated Soviet Russia. At the end of November 1929, they began to organize various provocative gatherings. The responsible young communists wore red shirts and added Russian Communist Party symbols, appearing arrogant and oppressive. This move greatly displeased the farmers, who decided to rise up and strike at the Communist Party. This is the origin of the Lapua Movement. However, the initial riots were relatively restrained. Although the Communist Party members suffered insults, there were no casualties.

After the Lapua farmers first clashed with the Communist Party, many patriotic organizations were established throughout Finland, demanding that the government adopt strict methods to suppress communism. For a time, an anti-communist atmosphere enveloped the entire country. The name of the Lapua Movement became widely known.

Commercial News

Financial and Gold Markets Rise Sharply

The trend is moving forward step by step. Yesterday, on the 30th, the gold market situation was extremely sharp, continuing to show a peak, exceeding the 570 taels threshold. The upward trend advanced frequently, and the deinventory was swift. The total turnover for both morning and afternoon sessions reached 16 taels. However, only two or three taels were recorded at the beginning of the morning session. The fluctuations only started in the afternoon, fluctuating between four and five taels. Both the official and unofficial exchange rates showed a strong upward trend, shrinking twice, with each reduction accounting for two price levels. Dealers actively bought, mainly British gold. The floor trading was quite active, with demand exceeding supply. Major players such as Taikang, Runyuanxing, Yongxin, Hengyifeng, and Yong etc. all pursued purchases, with some covering short positions. However, Yuanmaoyong and Hengxing Shunli etc. all sold. It rose high early in the morning, likely due to the fall in overseas silver prices. Afterwards, there was a surge in buyers, and the exchange rate rose, creating a sense of great prosperity. By noon, it had already exceeded 70 yuan. Later in the afternoon, Taikang Runyuanxing, Yongjin, and Yong etc. continued to buy tirelessly, while Hengxing Shunli, Wanxing etc. continued to sell positions. When the market reached its initial peak and then leveled off, it had risen to over 77 yuan. It was mainly due to the tight exchange rate. Therefore, settlement was very active. Afterwards, it suddenly turned lax. As a result, the confidence dropped. There was a sharp drop of five or six taels, a sudden and vast wave. The last price was within 73 taels, mainly because today (October 1st) is a holiday. Small retailers sold off in various ways to break even.

The initial market showed its edge. The November contract rose 1.8 yuan from the morning opening price to 561.8 yuan. Large silver bars shrank by 125, and silver prices went down slightly by half a cent. Afterwards, it became even stronger. Xinhng, Yuanxing, Yongtai, Kangrun, and contended to buy to cover short positions. Therefore, when the first order was announced, it was around 67 taels, and the listed price had shrunk by 25, with the US dollar at half a yuan and the Japanese gold adding 1.5 cents. Then it was added to 7.78 yuan. The wheat merchants absorbed the November British gold at 7 pence and 3125. After a while, it decreased by slightly more than one tael to 66.23 yuan. But the buyers were quite concentrated. Then the December British gold was offered by Sumitomo Chung Wan at 7 pence and 375. Soon it was absorbed into the January 4375 contract. At around 10 o'clock, the price rose to 69.2 yuan. Later, Zhifeng Yongshunli etc. all sold, and the price dropped by slightly more than three taels. But there was a one tael or several qian callback. At 10:50, it was calculated at 65.78 yuan. Suddenly, at 11 o'clock, it rose again, quite colorful. Because the bank's appetite for British gold was still good, and Taikang, Runxinhng etc. continued to buy non-stop, the situation became like a rising storm, reaching five or six taels and breaking through the 70 tael mark. By 11:30, it had reached 71.8 yuan. Afterwards, there was a one-tael reversal, and when the noon market closed at 71.4 yuan, it was re-pulled up by several qian to 72 taels. The disclosed price had been changed to 616.2 yuan, with the listing price increased by 1.5 cents. The initial pressure was around 50 taels, and at noon it was more than 44 taels.

Money Shops' Banknote Settlement Delayed by One Day

Money shops usually settle their accounts daily, but due to the unstable situation and the prevalence of robberies, it was decided to change the settlement to the 2nd and 26th of each lunar month, canceling the usual daily settlement. After the adoption of the Gregorian calendar this year, the settlement days were changed to the 2nd and 16th of each month. However, due to the Mid-Autumn Festival holiday, which falls on the 1st, the settlement on the 2nd will be combined, inevitably making it exceptionally busy. Therefore, there is a proposal to delay it by one day. The announcement from their association is recorded below: To our esteemed colleagues in the North Market, regarding the collection and payment of banknotes, it has been decided that the 2nd and 16th of each lunar month will be the settlement dates. Since the adoption of the Gregorian calendar this year, the 2nd and 16th of each month will be the settlement dates. It was proposed at the second regular meeting on March 26th, 18th year, that the settlement of banknotes on August 16th coincides with the Mid-Autumn Festival holiday, resulting in accumulated settlements. Accountants and warehouse staff often make mistakes due to being rushed. It was proposed to change the settlement to the 17th, which was previously decided. This year, it is tentatively set that October 1st is the Mid-Autumn Festival. The settlement of banknotes on the 2nd also coincides with the holiday, similar to the previous case. The settlement of banknotes on the 2nd should be changed to the 3rd to avoid errors. As this concerns industry regulations, this is specially announced for your information and compliance, etc. It is heard that the Market Committee also agreed that this time the settlement on the 2nd will be handled on the 3rd, and the settlement on the 3rd will be combined and handled on the 4th. Delaying it by one day will allow for a more relaxed and unhurried process, avoiding errors, etc.

Grand Delivery of Flour in September

411,000 Bags Delivered by Local and Foreign Manufacturers and Warehouses

In September, due to the quiet sales to customers and the smooth arrival of wheat, the production of each factory increased invisibly. The factories felt that they had to wait for the inventory to be sold, and they felt that there was no need to hedge the inversion of the market. Not only the small and medium-sized factories in this city are in this situation, but also those who joined the standard from foreign ports have delivered warehouse receipts, which shows that the abundance of inventory is undeniable. Wheat Imports to Begin Inspection

Factories Suffer Hidden Losses Due to Poor Quality Goods

Applying for Inspection is Essential

Total Inventory in Shanghai Reaches Over 300,000

All Subsequent Imports Must Undergo Inspection

The Shanghai Agricultural Product Inspection Office of the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining, considering that the quality of agricultural products has a great relationship with the livelihood of farmers and the needs of society, has learned that there are many flour factories in this city, and the annual purchase of wheat from foreign ports is very large. Local vendors and inland traders often have the bad habit of mixing mud and debris for petty profits. Without inspection, it is impossible to promote the improvement of agricultural products. It is heard that the office has prepared for this inspection and decided that from October 1st, all imports by train, ship, or boat must be inspected by the office before they can be sold. If the goods are of poor quality, they will be returned in a row and will not be allowed to unload. As for the wheat previously in storage, the director of the Miscellaneous Grain Association, Ye Huijun, has agreed with the office to limit the registration from the 1st to the 5th by the traders themselves for consideration. Therefore, the quality of wheat products after this will be a new look.

Youth Land

Impressions of a Northern Tour

— Su Ling

(9) Night in Harbin

"Night in Harbin" is a pantomime by Chen Ningqiu, depicting the misery of a nation of exiles in a foreign land. Before I even arrived in Harbin, the Huaguang Troupe performed it at the Huaguang Theater.

Mr. Chen told me that the performance of this pantomime was quite successful, especially in the stage design. The changes in lighting added a lot of mood to the play, thanks to the stage of the Huaguang Theater.

The plot involves three exiled beggars, one carrying a guitar, one with a mandolin, and one playing a small drum, standing on the bustling streets of this foreign land. Snow is falling, and in the cold wind, they tremble, using their frozen hands to play old, broken instruments. The mournful melodies scatter in the frigid air, amidst the bustling city, the snowflakes, and the cold glow of the streetlights... Yet, the people of this foreign land, the fashionable noblewomen, the pot-bellied shop owners... shuttle past these three exiles. They all seem not to see these three ethnic outcasts, not to hear the trembling melodies, and the sound of the small drum, as if a heart is quivering. They shuttle along their way, the women smiling and laughing, the men waving their canes.

The lights of the coffee shop gradually brighten, changing into various colors from bright to gradually dimming. Now, the streetwalkers are becoming increasingly scarce and gradually disappearing. The snow falls heavier and dances in the cold wind. The three beggars, pitiful, their melodies silenced, hungry, frozen, these homeless people finally collapse and sleep in the snow, trembling. It is late at night, and the cold wind is so desolate. At this time, the stern police come, waving small batons, using their feet to drive them away…

The lights of the coffee shop have gone out. Except for the snow dancing in the cold wind, everything is still.

Mr. Chen's play is based on Central Avenue in Harbin. So, hearing "Night in Harbin," after he finished telling the play's content, he adjusted the strings of his guitar and played the tune that the three beggars played, the plaintive melody trembling in the cold night.

I came out from Mr. Chen's place, passing Central Avenue to return to my residence.

Suddenly, a familiar sound lured me. Oh, in the dark corner of that street end, isn't it? There stand the three characters from Mr. Chen's play. Ah, three exiled foreign beggars, silently, trembling, plucking frozen strings, the mournful tremolo echoing in the rustling of people's clothing as they pass by.

Returning, I picked up a useless canvas and, under the light, painted these three beggars. Moreover, I added a small black dog, with the night shadow of this northern city as the background.

I titled this painting "Nocturne."

Jinda Female Students Preparing for Autonomous Association

— Kun

The National Jinan University, both the university and middle school divisions, has over two hundred female students. There has never been an autonomous organization. Recently, Zhang Wenzhu and Wu Feng initiated a call for all female students to discuss and decide to organize an autonomous association. With the permission of the school's moral education committee and registration, a preparatory committee was formally established, and seven people, including Zhang and Wu, were elected as preparatory committee members. It is scheduled to complete preparations before the Double Tenth Festival, and then formally elect executive committee members and supervisory committee members. The group is named the National Jinan University Female Student Autonomous Committee. Its purpose is (1) to seek happiness for all female students, (2) to develop the autonomous abilities of female students, cultivate a spirit of service, and prepare for serving society in the future. The organization of the group takes the general assembly as the highest organ, the executive committee executes all affairs, and the supervisory committee is responsible for supervision and impeachment. Under the executive committee, various departments are established: (1) General Affairs Department, responsible for all daily work within the committee and responsible for economic management, (2) Hygiene Department, governing health matters, divided into three sections: (A) Laundry Section, (B) Food Affairs Section, (C) Investigation Section, each responsible for laundry food affairs, and investigating the cleanliness of various places, (3) Sports or Physical Education Department, promoting female student sports, improving female student physical education, divided into basketball, tennis, volleyball, table tennis, and track and field sections, each managing the relevant sports matters, (4) Newspaper and Magazine Department, requesting the school authorities to provide books, newspapers, and magazines in the female student dormitory as much as possible, arranged for observation, and the right to manage them belongs to this department, (5) Publishing Department, planning to publish a Jinan University female student magazine every month, and other irregular publications will be determined temporarily, (6) Art Department, divided into (A) Chinese Literature Discussion Group, (B) Western Literature Discussion Group, (C) Philosophy Research Society, (D) Embroidery and Drawing Research Society, students can join any one or several departments according to their wishes, conduct research after class, and invite consultants to guide them, (7) Science Department, divided into (A) Mathematics and Physics Research Society, (B) Radio Research Society, (C) Biology Research Society, also inviting experts to serve as consultants to guide them, (8) Sales Department, organizing a sales society, hiring people to bid and sell items, various stationery, cold food, and hot food are all sold, the society address is next to the female student dormitory, this is a general overview of the organization, the committee has one chairman, each department has one director, and several section chiefs, depending on the amount of department affairs, each section has four to eight administrative staff, the chairman and each committee member are elected by the general assembly of eleven people (including one chairman), and then the committee members mutually elect the directors of each department, and the section chiefs and administrative staff are hired by the executive committee proposed by the directors, the term of each position is one semester, and the universal suffrage system is used to re-elect after the term expires, the source of their economy is, in addition to the subsidies from the school authorities, all borne by the female students, approximately each person pays at least two yuan in membership fees each semester, it is heard that when the inaugural meeting was held, a declaration was issued, asking universities across the country to promote it, this move is truly a pioneering initiative in female student autonomy.

Jingwu Association's Travel

The Beisichuan Road Jingwu Association, in addition to actively promoting physical education on weekdays, also pays attention to travel matters. Therefore, there are always two or three large-scale travel organizations every month. The travel locations set for October are as follows: (1) Travel to Hangzhou from the afternoon of the 4th to the 6th, collecting a round-trip train fare of three yuan per person. If you want to take a special car from Hangzhou to Haining to watch the tide, an additional round-trip car fare of four yuan will be charged. Food and accommodation are at your own expense. (2) Travel to Suzhou on the Double Tenth Festival, departing by car at 6:00 am and returning to Shanghai that night, costing three yuan and forty cents per person, including train, lunch, and boat fees. (3) On the 26th, travel to Fanwangdu and Zhenru, at which time it is also planned to visit the Mint, Daxia University, the radio station of Jinan University, and Zhangjia Garden. Depart in the morning by Shanghai-Hangzhou express train, costing seven cents per person, including breakfast, lunch, and car fare. All those who wish to join must register with the association in advance.

Youth Land Submission Guidelines

(1) Articles should focus on discussions of youth issues, news of domestic and foreign schools or students, essays, descriptions of school life, essays, etc., and the style is not limited.

(2) Books are limited to those concerning youth issues.

(3) Photos that are qualified are those showing the youth's life (such as sports, travel, excursions, drama performances, speeches, gatherings, exhibitions, various competitions, etc.), school news, and youth movements, etc. Both individuals and groups are welcome.

(4) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

Page 23

Art World Manuscript Guidelines

(1) Manuscripts should be limited to news, commentary, and introductory articles concerning the latest art (painting, music, sculpture, architecture, drama, etc.) and literature both domestically and internationally.

(3) Photographs should be limited to recent portraits of domestic and international artists, their works, and various photographs related to the text.

(4) The number of words in each manuscript should not exceed 2,000.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(6) Do not write manuscripts horizontally, and avoid careless handwriting. Use as little Western text as possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not use blue ink to draw illustrations in the manuscript, and do not use colored paper. White paper and black ink should be used.

(8) Please indicate that submissions are for the attention of the Art World Editorial Department.

(9) Submitted manuscripts will not be returned whether or not they are published. If a return is required, it should be stated in advance, and sufficient postage stamps should be included.

(10) Payment for manuscripts is divided into three categories: four yuan, three yuan, and two yuan per thousand words. Payment for illustrations and photographs is the same. For special manuscripts, payment will be calculated separately.

Book and Newspaper Introduction Manuscript Guidelines

(1) Manuscripts should be limited to introducing the latest domestic and international publications. Apart from literary works, all books and newspapers on politics, economics, law, science, education, etc., are included. However, trivial books and newspapers will not be introduced.

(2) Illustrations should be limited to recent works by new domestic and international artists and illustrations related to the text.

(3) Manuscripts concerning textual research or studies of ancient Chinese books will not be published.

(4) Both illustrations and photographs are limited to those related to the text.

(5) The number of words in each manuscript should not exceed 3,000.

(6) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(7) Do not write manuscripts horizontally, and avoid careless handwriting. Use as little Western text as possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(8) Do not use blue ink to draw illustrations, and do not use colored paper. White paper and black ink should be used.

(9) Submitted manuscripts will not be returned whether or not they are published. If a return is required, it should be stated in advance, and sufficient postage stamps should be included.

(11) Payment for manuscripts is divided into three categories: three yuan, two yuan, and one yuan per thousand words. Payment for illustrations and photographs is the same. For special manuscripts, payment will be calculated separately.

Social News Manuscript Guidelines

(1) Manuscripts should be limited to news concerning science, industry, commerce, rural areas both domestically and internationally.

(2) Health, aviation, exploration, customs, or urban life. Illustrations should be limited to lyrical paintings about various aspects of social life.

(3) Photographs of seasons, landscapes, animals, plants, people, and news photography are acceptable. Photographs of beautiful women in seasonal landscapes are especially welcome.

(4) The number of words in each manuscript should not exceed 2,000.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(6) Do not write manuscripts horizontally, and avoid careless handwriting. Use as little Western text as possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not use blue ink to draw illustrations, and do not use colored paper. White paper and black ink should be used.

(8) Please indicate that submissions are for the attention of the Social News Editorial Department.

(9) Submitted manuscripts will not be returned whether or not they are published. If a return is required, please declare in advance.

(10) Payment for manuscripts is divided into three categories: three yuan, two yuan, and one yuan per thousand words. Payment for illustrations and photographs is the same. For special manuscripts, payment will be calculated separately.

Automobile News

Special Article

Car Style Name Compendium: Countries Have Established Uniform Names

— Ji Ren

Car body style names vary from country to country. Major car body manufacturers in England, France, and the United States have recently recognized the large number of products from various factories and the complexity of their names. Not only do the manufacturers lack standards, but it also makes it difficult for car owners to distinguish between them. Therefore, they initiated the compilation of a car style name compendium to establish standard names for each car.

Take the name "Coupe" as an example. Different countries have different interpretations. In the United States, "Coupe" is the name of a single-seat sedan. In France, "Coupe" refers to a type of convertible. In other countries, it may refer to another type of vehicle. From this, it can be seen that the differences in car names are so great that it is necessary to standardize them.

Comparing the car style name records compiled by car factories in England, France, and the United States, the French version is the most detailed and organized. Its compilation method is based on the position and number of doors and windows of 22 types of cars. The top and rear of this type of vehicle are equipped with movable parts, which can change into 54 types of car styles. One can recognize them at a glance. The disadvantage of the French name is that its naming is slightly specialized. While it is convenient for the factory, it is not easy for car owners and salespeople to remember.

Vehicles are divided into four categories: sedans, convertibles, open cars, and limousines. Lengthening the rear end of each style turns it into a sports car. Installing a movable roof on a limousine turns it into a semi-sedan.

The car name record compiled by the American Society of Automotive Engineers is simpler, but not very detailed. It includes 16 types of car styles, mostly sedans. There are ten basic styles, such as sports cars, small sedans, roadsters, open cars, sedans, and city cars. The others are variations of the standard style. As for limousines with chauffeur compartments, there are only two types. This type of car is most popular in Europe.

England is known for its open cars. There are also 20 types of car style names, which have been reviewed and approved by the British Engineering Standards Association. Among these 20 types, only four are sedans, and the rest are open cars. This shows the British people's love for air and scenery.

The British people's fondness for traveling by car or living in the countryside is also well-known. Throughout the year, cars loaded with daily necessities travel back and forth on the roads, which can be said to be a national custom of England.

The source of English and American car names originates from French. Although the pronunciation is the same, the meanings are different. As for car body construction, the United States has always been known for it. The total annual production volume is higher than that of car factories in other countries. However, in the past four or five years, Europeans have paid attention to this and advocated self-reliance, raising funds to expand the car body construction business in order to resist foreign goods. Therefore, the American car body construction business has been somewhat affected. However, with the large demand from General Motors and other factories in the United States, its business can still occupy the top position in various countries.

In recent years, car styles have been renewed daily, and progress has been accelerating. European car factories also emphasize the appearance of car styles and strive for their products to be affordable and beautiful. Therefore, they all have relatively complete mechanical equipment and use mechanical work for manufacturing. As a result, production has gradually become large-scale. However, they are not yet able to compete with American car factories.

Thirty-Five Years of American Automobile Development History

— Pei Gan

Mr. Krullers, General Manager of General Motors in China, said that in the past 35 years, the changes and improvements in automobile manufacturing have never stopped. The goal is to make cars increasingly perfect, with a combination of mechanical excellence, convenient driving, and aesthetic appearance. Now, let's compare an old car from the past with a 1930s car. The difference between ancestor and descendant is laughable. However, this old-style car has its own characteristics. Just because new cars have emerged in recent decades does not mean that the old-style cars of the past are completely worthless.

Mr. Krullers also said that since 1895, the United States has produced no fewer than 640 types of cars. However, in recent times, only 41 famous brands remain. In addition, only older people can vaguely remember one or two. New car drivers do not even know the names of these cars. However, these cars have made contributions to the history of automobile development. They have made it possible for standard-style cars to be sold to the general public at affordable prices. These hundreds of models have each sought their own way forward to solve the practical transportation business.

The United States is the largest automobile producer. The number of new cars produced each year varies from 51 to 1. However, no new models were introduced in 1897. But it is undeniable that the early products did not last long. Of the 136 types of cars produced before 1905, 11 still exist. Between 1905 and 1910, more than 129 types of cars were produced. Five of them are still in use today. In the following decade, 167 new styles were produced. Eleven of them can still be seen today and are regarded as predecessors in the automobile industry. In the decade after that, production decreased, with only 77 new cars being produced. Seven or eight of them are still seen on the market.

The periods with the most automobile style production were 1901, 1902, 1903, 1907, 1908, and 1916. The following table can

Paget-Komata Wins Water Surface Championship

— Ke Luo

The American speedboat speed competition was held in the Hudson River this year. Among them, there was a small 19-foot speedboat equipped with a Paget six-cylinder engine, which can travel at 132 miles per hour. The route from Albany to New York averaged 30.5 miles per hour. According to the driver, Mr. Jack, the Paget engine has great resistance, and the oiling and shifting functions are very good. Therefore, its victory this time is due to this engine.

American Small Austin Car Introduced

— Ding Zuze

The British-made Small Austin car has long been known for its lightness and convenience. It has been heard that there is also a Small Austin car being manufactured in the United States. At a time when gasoline prices are at their highest, car users want cars that save gasoline. This news is welcome.

The Small Austin car manufactured by American Austin Car Co. Inc. has only one type, and its name is American Austin.

The American Austin car is based on the structure of the British Austin car and is made with American materials. Its form is also American. Currently, the daily production volume is about 100 vehicles. There is only one type of two-seater, two-door sedan. Its shape is as shown in the attached figure. The American Austin car is the smallest car in America today. Each vehicle is worth 445 US dollars, delivered at the factory. The car weighs 1,130 pounds.

The engine of this car has four cylinders. The diameter of the engine cylinder is 2.2 inches, the stroke is 3 inches, and the exhaust volume is 45.6 cubic inches, with about 7 horsepower.

The car is 4 feet 5 inches wide, and the wheelbase is 6 feet 3 inches. It can turn around freely in a 31-foot-wide road without having to reverse.

This car has three forward speeds and one reverse speed. The fastest speed is 50 miles per hour. One gallon of gasoline can travel 40 miles. One tire can travel 20,000 to 40,000 miles.

The sales area of ​​this car is limited by the British Austin car factory to only the United States, Canada, and the West Indies. Sales to the Far East are not allowed. If you order directly from the factory, there are no restrictions.
